## Text Elements
OSTEP Learnings ^oBAdACok

      OS concepts rather than C for now ^a96fNHwX

1. Intro ^f5nHDVJp

On a basic level, when we run a program on computer,
the processor will FETCH, DECODE and EXECUTE a number of instructions
until the program comes to an end. ^DVpvOTnP

Von Neumann model ^Gh3WyhVd

However, we need to -
- make it easy to run programs (even allowing to seemingly run many at the same time)
- allow programs to share memory
- enable programs to interact with devices ^BSY8U0LO

The OS is responsible for ensuring the above,
thus making the system operate correctly, is easy to use and is efficient ^g1TiTNFi

Achieved through the 
technique of virtualization ^1fio908m

CPU ^aM7H6PRC

OS virtualizes resources i.e. -> ^vmtVjKJO

Physical resource ^wYBblxEw

transformed
to ^RUZd26Qn

Virtual version of itself ^xopLBgPb

CPU ^ZX7bEgzM

seemingly
many ^eG36rwgZ

CPU ^sJenMYDa

CPU ^Y6wdKr7F

CPU ^SIwPaco3

i.e. each program thinks it has infinite processing power ^u7T2UeBp

MEMORY ^xmTAxd99

MEM ^ChwhwrWk

seemingly
many ^2L1L58Ik

MEM ^ucHZ4xXR

MEM ^IMKouIkl

MEM ^D9n2IJ7G

i.e. each program thinks it has infinite memory ^yFsSXI0p

HDD/SSD ^RIuUW0zx

SSD ^PZRABIcc

seemingly
many ^pdFgrFO3

SSD ^0xHJmglo

SSD ^uzd48kY1

SSD ^Z9nyUK96

i.e. each program thinks it has infinite disk space ^bPxrmwN4

That is also why we refer to
OS as a virtual machine ^9OXxIMS8

How to make use of these OS virtualization features?? ^TFKt1I1D

To let OP interact with the OS (and indirectly with the compute resources)
i.e. tell it what to do with resources, OS provides certain APIs
These are called system calls ^Af4pGzFg

as the OS provides system calls to
run programs, access memory and devices, and other related actions,
we also sometimes say that the OS provides a standard library to applications ^9kJjfUeK

This virtualization allows 
many programs to -
- run (sharing CPU)
- concurrently access their own
  instructions and data
  (sharing memory)
- access devices
  (sharing disk and more)

Hence the OS is called as
a resource manager ^Z3C4McJq

CRUX
HOW, then does the 
OS achieve virtualization
of resources
- what mechanisms and policies
  are implemented
- what hardware support needed ^pcwsuzMK

Throughout the chapter,
we aim to answer these questions ^nGmgHNtt

lets understand the role of OS better
by understanding these 3 things with chapter code ^I4qgCF3F

Virtualizing the CPU ^KXYSania

Virtualizing the memory ^YmTXUjJh

Access disk via syscalls ^WfX60fHW

The OS implements certain mechanisms by enforcing certain policies
In this case, we the see the mechanism of running multiple programs at once
which is implemented by enforcing scheduling policy ^yHbt6Txp

The idea of doing many things at once raises certain questions like if many programs want to run, which one should run first?
these questions are addressed by the policies of the OS. which in turn help implement certain mechanisms ^VLGDN85c

Now that we looked at the role of OS,
lets take a look at goals to keep in mind
for implementing an OS from scratch ^1EjHLg31

Concurrency ^urLJf8cH

 Like any system built by humans, good
ideas accumulated in operating systems over time, as engineers learned
what was important in their design ^itvuvGtw

brief history of how operating systems developed. ^MvjuBZ3g

1. Just libraries ^j1AGrj8R

2. Protection ^qrbmT4C7

3. Multiprogramming ^UC76ZESl

simply exposed apis for commonly used functions.
instead of having every dev write low level I/O code
the OS provided apis for these, make dev life easier ^Cv1safXd

Ran one program at a time,
Thus the idea of batch processing i.e. 
operator will run a batch of jobs manually ^YRG2QDDK

The computer took the program, start executing,
but the operator sat idle till completion,
so at this point using computers was not interactive ^4PJIeRID

then devs learned that code ran on OS behalf 
(via apis by user) was special
It had control of devices and I/O, hence must be treated different
Thus the notion of protection -- Otherwise any malicious program can access this code,
and by extension, all of the devices can be controlled ^wJTa3o6Y

Hence exposing the file system as a lib api to anyone is bad ^oeB8A4QR

This led to the development of system calls
    Implemented as special hardware apis that do 2 things
    - jumps into the OS code
    - raise hardware privilege level ^9TwkBGqE

as opposed to the previous procedure call
this will work with special hardware
instructions and state.
Where we can have more control by enforcing certain policies?? ^KCUyYagA

User mode
(application code) ^bTmdfer1

Kernel mode
(OS code) ^PMm2FFuE

trap
hw
instruction ^0lGW3g5p

make
syscall ^DrUHXZVd

Device ^bFu0GT78

Device ^RcXjHWyi

Device ^Qsm4iFNy

I/O ^Tgzxi9W1

I/O ^XoXunju0

I/O ^M7nJxj6U

service the
request ^HeCVOGAY

return
from
trap ^EqLEourR

development took off
with minicomputer ^wKJ6eKm8

more affordable ->  ^0YthG706

one org one computer
v/s
same org, multiple groups, one computer ^QSUK7x8n

better utilization of resources -> ^I1ke1PPn

one job
v/s
many jobs loaded into memory and CPU switched
between them rapidly  ^Xoh19ghz

the idea was that
CPU fast -- IO slow
1 program running at a time -> issues IO req, waits to fulfill, wasting CPU time
WHY NOT RUN other program on CPU while first is waiting for IO ^Ug2WACmX

- memory issues motivated
    innovation in memory protection
- concurrency issues motivated
    innovation in concurrency policies and mechanisms
- ensuring correct code behavior in presence
    of interrupts was also a challenge ^351LBI1h

4. Modern computers ^8O8DFmtK

cheaper, faster and for the masses
-> the PC ^gzJpICWP

The people at the forefront of PCs in this era
unfortunately forgot some of the important lessons from the minicomputer era
- microsoft thought memory protection was not important
    causing malicious program to corrupt memory
- apple used coop job scheduling policy
    where one bad job stuck in an infinite loop would force reboot ^CZLNgjnK

They catched up later ^8BMrc7RJ

These ideas
continue to develop
even today ^ZKQtzJDV
